      <article class="blog-single-post theme-post-entry post-2251 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-design category-technology category-web-design category-web-development tag-css-3 tag-css3 tag-design tag-html-5 tag-html5 tag-jquery" id="post-2251">

        <div class="post-title-wrapper">
         <h1 class="post-title">
          Pure CSS3 Spiderman Cartoon w/ jQuery and HTML5  Look Ma, No Flash!
         </h1>
        </div>
        <div class="clear">
        </div>
        <div class="post-content-content">
         <blockquote>
          <p>
           <strong>
            Update: 10/11/2011
           </strong>
           <em>
            New Animation;
            <a href="//www.optimum7.com" target="_blank">
             Making Internet Marketing Fun with Wufoo and CSS3
            </a>
           </em>
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         <div class="alignleft">
          <p>
           <a href="//www.optimum7.com/css3-man">
            <img alt="" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-2290" height="239" src="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/CSS3-Man-1.jpg" title="CSS3-Man-1" width="250"/>
           </a>
          </p>
          <p>
           <em style="font-size: .85em; padding: 10px; background-color: #333; color: #fff; border-radius: 5px; moz-border-radius: 5px; webkit-border-radius: 5px;">
            Dont have CSS3 animation capable browsers?
            <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=T1C_iRpViV0" style="color: #ffffff !important;" target="_blank">
             Watch a video of the animation.
            </a>
           </em>
          </p>
         </div>
         <h2>
          Inspiration
         </h2>
         <p>
          Searching YouTube for inspiration I stumbled on to the intro of the classic 1967 spider-man cartoon series. While watching I realized that the animation was very basic. It was the paper doll sort of animation that lends itself perfectly to css3. Hmmm I could something like that with a little css3, I thought.
         </p>
         <h2>
          Character &amp; background art
         </h2>
         <h4>
          CSS3-MAN
         </h4>
         <div class="alignleft clearfix">
          <a href="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-a.jpg">
           <img alt="" class="size-thumbnail wp-image-2252" height="150" src="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-a-150x150.jpg" title="spidey-a" width="150"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <p>
          The character art was created in adobe illustrator and copy/pasted into photoshop for export. When designing a character for animation. Carefully plan all the pieces that will compose your character. I decided on simple shapes and built each part of the body separately, like a marionette. This allowed me to re-use some graphics. By building the character like a marionette. I was able to simplify the animation process.
         </p>
         <div class="alignright clearfix">
          <a href="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-b.jpg">
           <img alt="" class="size-thumbnail wp-image-2259" height="150" src="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-b-150x150.jpg" title="spidey-b" width="150"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <p>
          As previously stated, the graphics originated in illustrator. Vectors paths and points make it simple to adjust the artwork. For instance, If you need spidey looking up or down. Simply adjust the position of the eyes and webbing on the head shape to complete the illusion. You can clean up any extra lines by simply moving the point or deleting it.
         </p>
         <div class="alignleft clearfix">
          <a href="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-c.jpg">
           <img alt="" class="size-thumbnail wp-image-2260" height="150" src="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-c-150x150.jpg" title="spidey-c" width="150"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <p>
          Same applies for the torso, legs and arms. By adjusting the orientation of the chest design and belt we can fake the rotation of a 2d element. Moving the arms and/or legs a little behind and a little in front of the torso creates the illusion of a subtle 3rd dimension.
         </p>
         <h4>
          BACKGROUND
         </h4>
         <div class="alignright clearfix">
          <a href="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-d.jpg">
           <img alt="" class=" size-thumbnail wp-image-2261" height="150" src="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-d-150x150.jpg" title="spidey-d" width="150"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <p>
          The cityscapes were also created in illustrator. But they started as plain screen-grabs. I captured certain parts of the video as it played. Then pasted them into illustrator. I created another layer above the screen-grab. Drawing paths over the screen-grabs images. Using it like tracing paper. When graphics were done, I trashed the screen-grab layer.
         </p>
         <div class="alignleft clearfix">
          <a href="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-e.jpg">
           <img alt="" class=" size-thumbnail wp-image-2262" height="150" src="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-e-150x150.jpg" title="spidey-e" width="150"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <p>
          Just like the character. When creating these cityscape graphics you must think a little in advance about how the pieces must fit together. Background images used for scrolling and zooming should be 2 or 3 times wider and/or taller to allow for panning left, right, up, or down. The same applies for zooming in and out. Now we have our finished character and background graphics. We can begin setting up our graphics for animation.
         </p>
         <h2>
          Complex CSS3 character animation and rigging
         </h2>
         <h4>
          CHARACTER RIGGING
         </h4>
         <p>
          One of the trickiest parts to creating these css3 character animations is the rigging of joints or skeleton so that they hinge and rotate believably. The most important property is the transform-origin property. The transform-origin property uses x,y coordinates to determine the point from which animation or transformations occur. (If you want a full explanation of css3 animation properties please read my last article.) In order to determine the accurate transform-origin point for our arm and leg graphics were going to use a simple trick.
         </p>
         <div class="alignleft clearfix">
          <a href="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-f.jpg">
           <img alt="" class=" size-thumbnail wp-image-2263" height="150" src="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-f-150x150.jpg" title="spidey-f" width="150"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <p>
          Notice how the foot graphic (1) is much wider than the thigh graphic (2). It would be impossible to match up the transform-origin point on these two pieces.
         </p>
         <div class="alignright clearfix">
          <a href="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-g.jpg">
           <img alt="" class=" size-thumbnail wp-image-2264" height="150" src="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-g-150x150.jpg" title="spidey-g" width="150"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <p>
          However, If we match the width of the thigh (2) with the width of the foot (1) Thats it! By increasing the width of the canvas area of the thigh to match the width of the foot we can accurately match the rotation points of these hinges using the css3 transform-origin property. By giving the thigh image a wider canvas area we can move the thigh graphic left or right to line it up with the foot graphic.
         </p>
         <div class="alignleft clearfix">
          <a href="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-h.jpg">
           <img alt="" class=" size-thumbnail wp-image-2265" height="150" src="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-h-150x150.jpg" title="spidey-h" width="150"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <p>
          We can now ascertain that these two pieces will have the exact rotation points via css3 transform origin. By setting the transform-origin for foot to (x) number of pixels from the left we can guarantee that the foot will rotate from exactly where the bottom of the shin is located.
         </p>
         <div class="alignright clearfix">
          <a href="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-i.jpg">
           <img alt="" class=" size-thumbnail wp-image-2266" height="150" src="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-i-150x150.jpg" title="spidey-i" width="150"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <p>
          Now we can apply the same transform origin coordinates to the top of the leg div (which wraps around thigh &amp; foot). By rotating the leg div we rotate its children too. This means that the leg div rotates both the thigh and foot graphics at the same time. Mimicking the functionality of a skeleton. Which allows us to have the foot moving along its own rotation path while also rotating along the path of the whole leg. Its important to nest items because this allows you to have multiple animation paths without having to recalculate their position constantly. If I rotate the thigh and foot without first wrapping them in a leg div how would I also make the foot rotate upon the axis of the leg? It would be near to impossible. And it would look horrible. By nesting and breaking down the animations into their major body parts and just animating one major body part at a time and utilizing the animation of children I can achieve complex (for css) animation combinations. Creating the illusion of the character zooming in required that the images be created at a bigger size. Then implementing them into the html mark-up at a smaller size. There are two ways to do this. Using the scale transform property or using the image width property. By increasing the image width over a key-framed animation you give it the illusion of growing or zooming into the screen. We can make a 500 pixel wide image then insert it into the html at 5% of its size. We are then able to make it smaller or bigger by increasing the height or width via css3.
         </p>
         <h2>
          Complex Character Animation
         </h2>
         <div class="alignleft clearfix">
          <a href="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-j.jpg">
           <img alt="" class=" size-thumbnail wp-image-2267" height="150" src="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-j-150x150.jpg" title="spidey-j" width="150"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <p>
          When building a character composed of precisely placed elements. Being able to visually construct the character is essential. When we first place all the different pieces for our character into the html. They are all jumbled up together. Firefox 3.x has implemented css3 moz-transform-origin and moz-rotate. Which means I can use firebug developer tool to visually position the characters body parts where they belong. This makes setting up the start and end positions/rotations for the characters pose simple. To begin, we set up the characters body parts in the start position. I just adjust the values to where I need them in order to get the proper first position. I visually adjust the rotation and position values of the graphic using firebug.
         </p>
         <div class="alignleft clearfix">
          <a href="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-L.jpg">
           <img alt="" class=" size-thumbnail wp-image-2268" height="150" src="//www.optimum7.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/spidey-L-150x150.jpg" title="spidey-L" width="150"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <p>
          This allows me to gain pixel perfect precision over where I want the graphic placed. Using firebug like this takes the guesswork out of animating something as technical as different body parts. I just visually adjust the values to where I need them to get the proper first position. We then place those coordinates into the css. Now we have to figure out the end positions for our animation. We use the same technique. Adjusting the values to accommodate the end position and plug those values into the css as well. Finally, I place these values in the start and end parts of the css3 keyframe function. Then we check the animation in webkit. Webkit does the rest of the magic on its own. By using firefox and chrome together I was able to find the start and end points to each body part and then allow @keyframes to fill in the blanks.
         </p>
         <h2>
          Putting it all together
         </h2>
         <p>
          Believe it or not, the biggest road block I encountered when creating this css3 cartoon was switching the scenes at the correct moment to coincide with the css3 animation. I used jquerys built in delay function to flip through the scenes and activate the next scene. As Im writing this I realize that I probably could have pulled off the scene switching with css3 animation as well. But Im not sure  as I havent thought it all the way through. We used the built in animation delay function on css3 to begin animating the scenes just as they were activated by jQuery. Another challenge I had was that I had no control over when the animation started. I had to preload all the elements. Because there was no way to start all of the animations on just one click throughout the entire flick. And if all the elements are not loaded when the animations start running it gets jumpy. Including the audio soundtrack was almost too easy. I just inserted a simple html 5 audio tag. (Gosh, Im falling for html 5).
          <a href="http://anthonycalzadilla.com">
           <em>
            Anthony Calzadilla
           </em>
          </a>
          <em>
           is a real cool dude at
          </em>
          <a href="//www.optimum7.com">
           <em>
            Optimum7.com
           </em>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          You can see examples of our
          <a href="//www.optimum7.com/custom-programming">
           custom programming work using css here
          </a>
          .
         </p>

             <span class="reply">
              <a aria-label="Reply to Francis Adu-Gyamfi" class="comment-reply-link" href="/internet-marketing/web-development/pure-css3-spiderman-ipad-cartoon-jquery-html5-no-flash.html?replytocom=260#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-260", "260", "respond", "2251" )'>

            <div class="comment-wrapper">
             <div class="comment-autor">
              <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/97f1028b05e086097780af48dfa173ab?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/97f1028b05e086097780af48dfa173ab?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" width="80"/>
             </div>
             <div class="comment-text">
              <p>
               Great work. Really shows off what CSS3 and a fair amount of Javascript can accomplish. However, if no one will say it, I will.
              </p>
              <p>
               80  100 hours makes it no easier than doing this in Flash or JavaFX. 1.7MB total weight, still makes it a tad heavier than what might be possible in a well optimized Flash product.
              </p>
              <p>
               Personally after a whole lot of reading, I am not sure what the goal of CSS3 and HTML5 is meant to be at this point. Is it supposed to provide just an improved document handling system or some major framework for media oriented products? All in all, plugin based RIAs will die at some point, but until then, long live the RIA wars
              </p>
             </div>
            </div>
            <div class="clear">
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>

It seems like I need to be a full-time programmer to do this in HTML5.

             <div class="comment-text">
              <p>
               Can not believe how many flash guys dont get it:
               <br/>
               This is a first cut. There will be animation toolkits, languages  see processing.js, ides  see atlas and bespin  all targeting HTML5. Clearly, right now, its easier to use Flash the IDE for delivering this kind of animation.
               <br/>
               But getting rid of the choke hold on innovation that Adobe currently holds is priceless.
              </p>
              <p>
               Flash the runtime and .swf the format are certainly on life support.  Flash the IDE will  almost certainly be moving to target HTML5 as we speak, and will survive, but as a more equal competitor.
               <br/>
               It might even be possible for .swf the format to survive, if the player is implemented in javascript using canvas.
              </p>
             </div>

              <p>
               Truthfully, I -am- excited about the new capabilities of HTML5 and CSS3. Like any web developer, Ive been awaiting this for too, too long. But its 10 years late, and other technologies (like flash) are already light years ahead of it, and still moving way faster by the time this is even a standard.
              </p>
             </div>
            </div>
            <div class="clear">
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
         </li>

              <p>
               Interesting possibilities. But where will Flash be when the HTML5 standard is completed and implemented (expected in 2022)?
              </p>
              <p>
               Some developers have overused Flash by a considerable amount. But some of what Flash can do today wont be available in HTML5 in 2022. What Flash did for us more than anything else is gave us a single technology to do our creative work once and run it on most any platform, out of the box. Apples just set us all back 10 to 15 years.
              </p>
              <p>
               All Adobe would have to do to pull Apple back to reality is discontinue Adobe software on the Mac. The market for the Mac would dry up overnight. As a loyal Mac user since 1987 (starting with an SE), I hope Adobe doesnt do it. But I wouldnt blame them if they did.
              </p>
              <p>
               Apples stranglehold on the iPhone/iPad product line drove me to the Android phone OS. With Googles purchase of On2, and the cooperation of Adobe and Google, we may soon see technology that blows the doors off of HTML5. Of course, who really knows?
              </p>
              <p>
               HTML has always been basic technology. Weve needed Pearl, PHP, ASP(X), ColdFusion, XML, DHTML, Javascript, CSS, etc. to make HTML actually DO something other than just display text and images. In twenty years, HTML still doesnt do much else. It displays video now in two browsers? Wow. Welcome to 1998.
              </p>

               <a class="url" href="http://www.nineteenfortyone.com" rel="external nofollow">
                Kris
               </a>
              </cite>
             </span>
             <span class="comment-date">
              May 11, 2010
             </span>
             <span class="reply">
              <a aria-label="Reply to Kris" class="comment-reply-link" href="/internet-marketing/web-development/pure-css3-spiderman-ipad-cartoon-jquery-html5-no-flash.html?replytocom=363#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-363", "363", "respond", "2251" )'>
               Reply 
              </a>
             </span>
            </div>
            <div class="clear">
            </div>
            <div class="comment-wrapper">
             <div class="comment-autor">
              <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/c056b7cc0ff75717cb53207749774177?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/c056b7cc0ff75717cb53207749774177?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" width="80"/>
             </div>
             <div class="comment-text">
              <p>
               Wow, this is really awesome.  Amazing.  Youve rekindled my excitement for HTML5 and CSS3.  Nice job and well done!
              </p>
              <p>
               For all of you who are saying this or that is better than the other:  Use the right tool for the job.  Yes, this animation could have been done better, faster, more widely available if done with Flash, but this is a proof of concept; A demonstration at where non-Flash technology is, and the direction in which its going.  Its not suggesting that one technology will replace the other.
              </p>
              <p>
               I expect HTML5 and CSS3 will continue to improve over the coming years, but Flash will always have its place.  We, as multimedia developers, have more tools to from which to choose.  Use the right tool for the job.  (I love the hammer and the screwdriver analogy.)
              </p>
             </div>
            </div>
            <div class="clear">
            </div>

             </div>
             <div class="comment-text">
              <p>
               This is a great example of how all of the hype and chatter about html5 is so ridiculous. Ok, kudos to you for taking the time to make this. But, as has been stated, this is primitive beyond belief compared to what Flash is capable of. By the time html5 reaches the place where Flash is (at least 5 years) Adobe will have Flash running circles around it. Theres also no decent authoring tools for html5 and, again, when they arrive they wont be able to do the things that Flash can do NOW. html5 has its place for sure, it is better to use it for certain things but you are not going to replace the robust features and performance of Flash for doing animation and complex interactivity.
              </p>
             </div>

             </div>
             <div class="comment-text">
              <p>
               None of these comments speak to the true point that authoring in flash is expensive. Yes Adobe practically gives it product away to students, only to lock them in for years by updating the platform every year with a new upgrade fee. The real benefit to this example is that the author used open tools with very minimum start-up fee. For him to create this with Adobe it would cost him $500 US just to draw the animation, tack on CSS &amp; flash authoring he is at $2000 not including a machine powerful enough to run it.
              </p>
              <p>
               Contrary to the Flash FUD in these comments the Internet is about interactivity which means the more people enabled to communicate the better the medium will become. Flash has its place in that purpose just as HTML5 will have its place.
              </p>
             </div>

              </p>
              <p>
               Anyone actually in the industry should see this as a great first step into not getting rid of Flash entirely (because that will never happen), but getting rid of it where its cumbersome.  I started my career relying heavily on Flash for interactivity and now develop 100% of my interactivity with AJAX because its just easier to work on, expand, fix, troubleshoot, hand off to someone else to work on, and scale up or down.  My bosses likes that because
               <br/>
               1.  They dont have to buy another Flash license and
               <br/>
               2.  Because the less time spent on development means the less money he has to spend.
              </p>
              <p>
               Not to degenerate into another Flash vs. HTML5 argument, my point is that while this animation does suck because its basically nothing but a bunch of fundamental motion tweens from Flash5, the fact that its being done entirely client side without any plug-ins is extraordinary and stands on its own.
              </p>
              <p>
               This is pretty god damn impressive if you ask me.
              </p>
             </div>
            </div>
            <div class="clear">
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
         </li>

            <div class="comment-wrapper">
             <div class="comment-autor">
              <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/e76fb45ebc687edb5b5d16a865e6b599?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/e76fb45ebc687edb5b5d16a865e6b599?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" width="80"/>

             <div class="comment-text">
              <p>
               Very Very impressive!
              </p>
              <p>
               Everything starts somewhere (including flash) and here comes reality! Unfortunately for flash dudes, we understand they feel threatened by the capabilities of html5/css3 catching up.
              </p>
              <p>
               Bill Gates was quoted in 1981 saying No one will need more than 637 kb of memory for a personal computer
               <a href="http://en.wikiquote.org/wiki/Bill_Gates" rel="nofollow">
                http://en.wikiquote.org/wiki/Bill_Gates
               </a>
               . He later ate his words.
              </p>
              <p>
               DONT STOP IMPROVING. I believe flash is almost at the end of the line for four main reasons:
              </p>
              <p>
               1. Technologies keep changing as soon as you think you have it all figured out, something else crawls out of the woodwork.
               <br/>
               2. Too many competitors of Adobe Flash and Lots of variations for it plus better products for coding flash now exists that use different raw materials (something that was unthinkable two years ago.) Different raw materials equal different product at the end of the day. Different product means different rules of the game.
               <br/>
               3. Although computers and other digital electronic devices that have RAM in them continue to be more powerful and are growing bigger and better, so are applications and OSs memory requirements for them. No where in history including recent history does it even hint that bigger RAM translates to means that applications will perform better. That is just but a consequence. Application developers require more RAM so they can help users do more (pushing the RAM boundaries). More is not necessarily better. Better product is a result of better workmanship/skills (which by the way, depends so much on the tools used). css3 uses RAM better (not the other way round -&gt; better RAM). Its the Most likely to be the one that gets adopted in the future as the tool of choice. Applications are the ones that push RAM not vice versa. Gadgets that show flash better is because the codec are available free to the manufacturers (more of a business reason than a technical one) and support provided via subscription (which hurts in the long run.) So Java and Flash were adopted for the same reason: Code once, run everywhere (cross-platform capability.)
               <br/>
               4. Remember corporations are still competing. Check out websites for the top or best performing companies, firms, institutions, etc, or serious firms like NOKIA (e-commerce sites), GOOGLE, NASDAQ, YAHOO, government sites, etc that you know of. This are the guys who pay money, and none of them will pay anyone to play with their information on the screen (and especially their clients. Try working with them). Check out their code: HTML! or at least most part of their pages are. If flash is available, its carefully used or used responsibly (meaning only where absolutely necessary: i.e. only where html/css or java cannot go for now). Bandwidths are important even if they come almost free. Pages have to load faster. People want information when they want it (not wait for it); They also want it the way they want it (more like the way they expect it). And they want that information to behave they way they want it to (like when they want to save a pages for later reference  which mostly happens offline). With so much information on the internet, people have
               <b>
                very
               </b>
               little time to check out all of the information on one website. They want to move on if they cant see it there, or at least see a pointer.
              </p>
              <p>
               To close it up, Anthony Calzadilla is one important dude on the internet pointing us to the next step in www which is already there. Hes in the footsteps of Tim Berners-Lee when you choose to see things clearly. Its a choice.
              </p>
             </div>
            </div>

              <p>
               I can answer why HTML5, CSS3, and JavaScript has to develop to the point where they can replace Flash. Flash is not free nor opensource. lts a paid thing. Some of us still cant afford to buy the ability to program in flash. Adobe owns Flash. The world owns HTML5, CSS3, and JavaScript. The world can create away without paying royalty fees and other fees that poor developers cant afford. Thats why HTML5 and CSS3 need to be developed more. Its why those 2 and JavaScript needs to be developed more so that they can do more without taking so much resources.
              </p>
              <p>
               Currently, there is even works to make JavaScript capable of MMORPGs. Its the wave of the future  to improve whats available so that no one is left behind in the dust.
              </p>
             </div>
            </div>
            <div class="clear">
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>

             <div class="comment-text">
              <p>
               If you could create it from scratch in Flash in an hour, its because youve used Flash many, many times before. This is the first time something like this has been done, so dont try to compare the two.  It represents the possibility that complex animation can be done without a $700 program AND a browser plugin.  I understand people who have taken the time to learn Actionscript will be upset that there could be an Open future with options other than Flash, but things evolve.  Put that energy toward learning a new language or just get the most out of Flash while you can, Im sure it will never go away completely.  Either way, please stop whining.
              </p>
              <p>
               Personally, knowing Actionscript myself, I hope it gets replaced with a more organized language.  8 lines of code to put a link on a button is just unnecessary.
              </p>
              <p>
               Anyway, really excellent work!  Truly inspiring.
              </p>

               <p>
                Hi Dave,
                <br/>
                Yes avoid using positioning values for animation. so instead of using absolute position values to move your object around, you want to use the translate3d(x,y,z) syntax, this triggers the built-in hardware acceleration in iOS devices
                <a href="http://mir.aculo.us/2010/06/04/making-an-ipad-html5-app-making-it-really-fast/" rel="nofollow">
                 http://mir.aculo.us/2010/06/04/making-an-ipad-html5-app-making-it-really-fast/
                </a>

          <div class="comment-container">
           <div class="comment-box">
            <div class="comment-info">
             <span class="coment-autor-name">
              <cite class="fn">
               geoff
              </cite>
             </span>
             <span class="comment-date">
              April 18, 2011
             </span>
             <span class="reply">
              <a aria-label="Reply to geoff" class="comment-reply-link" href="/internet-marketing/web-development/pure-css3-spiderman-ipad-cartoon-jquery-html5-no-flash.html?replytocom=1074#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-1074", "1074", "respond", "2251" )'>
               Reply 
              </a>
             </span>

            <div class="clear">

            <div class="comment-wrapper">
             <div class="comment-autor">
              <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/b46d3f6165245f3e5a9c3a12387ff2a9?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/b46d3f6165245f3e5a9c3a12387ff2a9?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" width="80"/>
             </div>
             <div class="comment-text">
              <p>
               If you are trying to make the statement that this can overtake flash I would say you have to be kidding right. I have worked since 1998 in flash with quite a number of projects along with MANY other languages. I am presently working in 5, jquery, and css. Flash is as powerful as it gets on the front end with its OOP technology not to mention its ability to produce movie like motion graphics. I find it insulting to think that there are people actually purporting that these 3 technologies have what it takes. As someone mentioned in this post the right tool for the right job. While these 3 can do some things, they fall incredibly short of actually producing an RIA. I have seen this type of posturing before when some group has an agenda they want to push, they fabricate claims and get a following of people who dont know any better or also have a wish list they want fulfilled. It is just this kind of bickering that holds up progress of the web. a few months ago Steve Jobs made a claim about flash being an energy sucker on the IPHONE and problematic in other areas. People bought in to the hype. Along comes the Android platform and debunks his statement. Jobs would not allow flash developers the ability to tap into the OS and so he hamstrung any possibility of flash developers  improving certain aspects of a program. Oh and did anyone give thought to Apple being the pusher for 5 technology? He wants to take marketshare from Adobe and get more people on to his proprietary app store. 5 has its place and so does Flash. Lets get on with it!
              </p>
             </div>
            </div>
            <div class="clear">
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
         </li>

         <!-- #comment-## -->
         <li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1">
          <div class="comment-container">
           <div class="comment-box">
            <div class="comment-info">
             <span class="coment-autor-name">
              <cite class="fn">
               <a class="url" href="http://www.hubumedia.com" rel="external nofollow">
                heyvern
               </a>
              </cite>
             </span>
             <span class="comment-date">
              September 14, 2011
             </span>
             <span class="reply">
              <a aria-label="Reply to heyvern" class="comment-reply-link" href="/internet-marketing/web-development/pure-css3-spiderman-ipad-cartoon-jquery-html5-no-flash.html?replytocom=2237#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-2237", "2237", "respond", "2251" )'>
               Reply 
              </a>
             </span>
            </div>
            <div class="clear">
            </div>
            <div class="comment-wrapper">
             <div class="comment-autor">
              <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/384eb72d02b527d4fdef563622e5925c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/384eb72d02b527d4fdef563622e5925c?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" width="80"/>
             </div>
             <div class="comment-text">
              <p>
               Many who argue about HTML5 being inferior to Flash are concerned about the investment both in knowledge and the application. This happens to everyone in any job. When a new technology makes your existing skill set less valuable or less critical to producing a product or service you are inclined to find problems with the new bad thing. From robots building cars to desktop publishing.
              </p>
              <p>
               I saw this happen in the print industry. When desktop publishing was just starting out, the businesses who had to do offset printing from computer files fought print designers like myself tooth and nail. They blocked us at every step. They said computer files were inferior, that the knowledge they had was far superior and that the computer could never handle trapping or full color separations using traditional analog photographic film processes. Keep in mind the people who did this stuff spent years learning those skills. They were right. It was a priceless skill gained over years of experience.
              </p>
              <p>
               Needless to say, the print shops who refused to accept our computer generated files or printing films failed because they didnt or couldnt afford to invest in the equipment and knowledge needed to support the new technology. I saw many of these shops close down very quickly because they couldnt compete.
              </p>
              <p>
               Flash is still better or faster than HTML5 right now but uh wake up and smell the coffee! A very short time ago HTML5 DIDNT EXIST. Most browsers didnt support ANY HTML5 features and barely supported most of the HTML 3 or 4 specs consistently or at all.
              </p>
              <p>
               HTML 5 has come so far so fast and will only improve. The writing is on the wall. Flash is not the only kid on the block. HTML5 is the new younger kid with some cool tricks that is going to steal Flashs job.
              </p>
             </div>
            </div>
            <div class="clear">
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
         </li>

                dem0n

             </span>
             <span class="reply">
              <a aria-label="Reply to dem0n" class="comment-reply-link" href="/internet-marketing/web-development/pure-css3-spiderman-ipad-cartoon-jquery-html5-no-flash.html?replytocom=3414#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-3414", "3414", "respond", "2251" )'>
               Reply 
              </a>
             </span>
            </div>
            <div class="clear">
            </div>
            <div class="comment-wrapper">
             <div class="comment-autor">
              <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/188516a016d7f5269b2f2c5c760c31bf?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/188516a016d7f5269b2f2c5c760c31bf?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" width="80"/>
             </div>
             <div class="comment-text">
              <p>
               Although I find it cool this was created using CSS3/jQuery/html5, youve got to admit that compared to the same animation being built in Adobes Flash CS5, this is just crappy. Im sorry, but the animations Ive seen to far built along these lines  although very cool as an experiment  just dont even come close to what Flash has to offer.
              </p>
              <p>
               As a webdesigner Im open to new possibilities, in fact, thats what I love about this line of work. The ever evolving technologies and techniques. Ive also been involved in alot of Flash vs HTML5 discussions, and knowing both Ive come to the conclusion that 90% of the people claiming HTML5 is a Flash killer dont have a clue what they are talking about.
              </p>
              <p>
               Frankly, even Flash developers are glad theres finally another method to play videos and mp3s without the use of flash. Its good to have a purely HTML version of those basics. The sad thing is, when many (without a better word for it) n00bs think Flash, they dont know anything better than oh, isnt that that thing we use to play videos and music?. Flash is s much more than that, and the ease with which you can build websites, games, animations and fullblown applications in Adobes Flash program just cant be challenged, and wont be for at least another 10-15 years.
               <br/>
               That said, like many others who actually are familiar with both technologies, I support the evolution of HTML5, CSS3 and jQuery totally, and instead of constantly bickering about HTML5 vs Flash (thanks Steve Jobs, you prick) you should realize they are just seperate technologies that can be used seperate or together. There is no conflict.
               <br/>
               HTML5/JS/jQuery are great for certain websites such as blogs &amp; community stuff, and Flash is great for advertising microsites, applications, games and animations that can be embedded within HTML sites.
              </p>
              <p>
               Anyone who believes CSS3 animation is a replacement for Flash animation really needs to try building animations in both before opening his mouth. Seriously. You cant compare the two.
               <br/>
               To build an animation in CSS3/Jquery/HTML5 you need to know all three languages beyond the basics. To build the same (and frankly even better) animation in Flash you need to spend maybe an hour or two watching a video tutorial on how motion tweens work. And thats it! Adobes Flash is so intuitive and easy to use. Just look at the sheer amount of animations and games created on sites like Newgrounds. Try coming close to that by typing pages of code trying to put together a (no offence) crappy animation like this.
              </p>
              <p>
               Again, I appreciate the experiment, which is a succes along the lines you were going for. But dont desperately try to compare it with Flash.
              </p>
             </div>
            </div>
            <div class="clear">
            </div>

           <div class="comment-box">
            <div class="comment-info">
             <span class="coment-autor-name">
              <cite class="fn">
               young developer
              </cite>
             </span>
             <span class="comment-date">
              April 12, 2012
             </span>
             <span class="reply">
              <a aria-label="Reply to young developer" class="comment-reply-link" href="/internet-marketing/web-development/pure-css3-spiderman-ipad-cartoon-jquery-html5-no-flash.html?replytocom=3655#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-3655", "3655", "respond", "2251" )'>
               Reply 
              </a>
             </span>
            </div>
            <div class="clear">
            </div>
            <div class="comment-wrapper">
             <div class="comment-autor">
              <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/b649bf4b97eb7e604ed153f94bfc35db?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/b649bf4b97eb7e604ed153f94bfc35db?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" width="80"/>
             </div>
             <div class="comment-text">
              <p>
               For those advising flash is better, Remember a stock standard install does not support flash in most cases and most people will upgrade their browser before they upgrade flash.
              </p>
              <p>
               In the world of web development one of the key features for cross platform is the ability to not have any dependencies in the way of something like flash.
              </p>
              <p>
               The browser/viewer/program should offer all the plugins/processors for the webpage without requiring a optional plugin which is just what flash is Optional.
              </p>
              <p>
               CSS &amp; HTML are foundations, libs like jQuery are also making there way into the foundations of javascript
              </p>
              <p>
               Remove HTML and flash does not exist in the web community
               <br/>
               Remove CSS and styling for websites does not exist
               <br/>
               These are the two base items that are used for this purpose and for this reason alone should always be expanded until they are replaced  Which will never be by flash. As for the comment of flash not being beaten by anything else for 10 years.. It already has been when you consider the factors between the applications of use.
              </p>
              <p>
               Also dealing with the ability to modify your css/html/javascript with server side processing is something that flash does not exactly offer in ease
              </p>
              <p>
               I could personally continue so many arguments in this way but for those who are stuck to an old way will always have their preference But for people who understand large term projects and expandability they do choose to build websites with the technologies they are based on..
              </p>
              <p>
               Regards,
               <br/>
               Brad M
              </p>
             </div>
            </div>

  <script>
   jQuery(function ($) {
		$(".jump-links a[href^='#']").on('click', function(e) {
			e.preventDefault();
			var hash = this.hash;
			$('body, html').animate({
				scrollTop: $(hash).offset().top-144
			}, 600, function(){
				if(history.pushState) {
					history.pushState(null, null, hash);
				}
				else {
					location.hash = hash;
				}
			});

		});
	});
  </script>
